# Architecture Q&A: Terraform Plan/Apply Pipeline

**Repository:** hashicorp/terraform
**Task Type:** Architecture Q&A (investigation only — no code changes)

## Background

Terraform's `terraform plan` command builds a dependency graph of all resources in the configuration, resolves providers, and computes the diff between desired state and current state. This process involves multiple layers: CLI command parsing, backend operation execution, graph construction via a series of transformers, concurrent graph walking, and provider plugin communication for diff computation.

## Questions

Answer ALL of the following questions about Terraform's plan execution pipeline:

### Q1: Command to Context

When a user runs `terraform plan`, how does the CLI command reach the core planning logic? Specifically:
- How does `PlanCommand.Run()` in `internal/command/plan.go` delegate to the backend?
- How does the backend create and invoke `terraform.Context.Plan()`?
- What are the key fields of `PlanOpts` that control plan behavior (mode, targets, force-replace)?

### Q2: Graph Construction Pipeline

How does `PlanGraphBuilder` construct the dependency graph for a plan operation?
- What is the role of the `Steps()` method and how does the sequence of `GraphTransformer` stages build the graph?
- Specifically, what do `ConfigTransformer`, `ReferenceTransformer`, and `AttachStateTransformer` each contribute?
- How does `ReferenceTransformer` analyze node references to add dependency edges between resources?

### Q3: Provider Resolution and Configuration

How are providers resolved, initialized, and configured during the plan walk?
- How does `EvalContext.InitProvider()` instantiate a provider plugin?
- At what point in graph execution is `ConfigureProvider()` called relative to resource planning?
- What is the role of `CloseProviderTransformer` in the graph lifecycle?

### Q4: Diff Computation per Resource

For a single managed resource instance, how does Terraform compute the planned changes?
- Trace the execution path from `NodePlannableResourceInstance.Execute()` through `managedResourceExecute()`
- How does the refresh phase (`refresh()`) synchronize with remote state before planning?
- How does the `plan()` method invoke the provider's `PlanResourceChange` RPC to compute the diff?
- What determines whether a resource is marked for create, update, replace, or delete?

## Output Requirements

Write your answer to `/logs/agent/investigation.md` with the following structure:

    18→type PlanCommand struct {
    19→	Meta
    20→}
    21→
    22→func (c *PlanCommand) Run(rawArgs []string) int {
    23→	// Parse and apply global view arguments
    24→	common, rawArgs := arguments.ParseView(rawArgs)
    25→	c.View.Configure(common)
    26→
    27→	// Propagate -no-color for legacy use of Ui.  The remote backend and
    28→	// cloud package use this; it should be removed when/if they are
    29→	// migrated to views.
    30→	c.Meta.color = !common.NoColor
    31→	c.Meta.Color = c.Meta.color
    32→
    33→	// Parse and validate flags
    34→	args, diags := arguments.ParsePlan(rawArgs)
    35→
    36→	// Instantiate the view, even if there are flag errors, so that we render
    37→	// diagnostics according to the desired view
    38→	view := views.NewPlan(args.ViewType, c.View)
    39→
    40→	if diags.HasErrors() {
    41→		view.Diagnostics(diags)
    42→		view.HelpPrompt()
    43→		return 1
    44→	}
    45→
    46→	// Check for user-supplied plugin path
    47→	var err error
    48→	if c.pluginPath, err = c.loadPluginPath(); err != nil {
    49→		diags = diags.Append(err)
    50→		view.Diagnostics(diags)
    51→		return 1
    52→	}

    18→// PlanGraphBuilder is a GraphBuilder implementation that builds a graph for
    19→// planning and for other "plan-like" operations which don't require an
    20→// already-calculated plan as input.
    21→//
    22→// Unlike the apply graph builder, this graph builder:
    23→//
    24→//   - Makes its decisions primarily based on the given configuration, which
    25→//     represents the desired state.
    26→//
    27→//   - Ignores certain lifecycle concerns like create_before_destroy, because
    28→//     those are only important once we already know what action we're planning
    29→//     to take against a particular resource instance.

    34→	// State is the current state

    38→	// given by the caller, which we'll resolve into final values as part
    39→	// of the plan walk.
    40→	RootVariableValues InputValues
    41→
    42→	// ExternalProviderConfigs are pre-initialized root module provider
    43→	// configura

   112→func (b *PlanGraphBuilder) Build(path addrs.ModuleInstance) (*Graph, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {
   113→	log.Printf("[TRACE] building graph for %s", b.Operation)
   114→	return (&BasicGraphBuilder{

   116→		Name:  "PlanGraphBuilder",
   117→	}).Build(path)
   118→}

   136→		// Creates all the resources represented in the config

   140→// Plan generates an execution plan by comparing the given configuration
   141→// with the given previous run state.
   142→//
   143→// The given planning options allow control of various other details of the
   144→// planning process that are not represented directly in the configuration.
   145→// You can use terraform.DefaultPlanOpts to generate a normal plan with no
   146→// special options.
   147→//
   148→// If the returned diagnostics contains no errors then the returned plan is
   149→// applyable, although Terraform cannot guarantee that applying it will fully
   150→// succeed. If the returned diagnostics contains errors but this method
   151→// still returns a non-nil Plan then the plan describes the subset of actions
   152→// planned so far, which is not safe to apply but could potentially be used
   153→// by the UI layer to give extra context to support understanding of the
   154→// returned error messages.
   155→func (c *Context) Plan(config *configs.Config, prevRunState *states.State, opts *PlanOpts) (*plans.Plan, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {
   156→	plan, _, diags := c.PlanAndEval(config, prevRunState, opts)
   157→	return plan, diags
   158→}
   159→
   160→// PlanAndEval is like [Context.Plan] except that it additionally makes a
   161→// best effort to return a [lang.Scope] which can evaluate expressions in the
   162→// root module based on the content of the generated plan.
   163→//
   164→// The scope will be nil if the planning process doesn't complete successfully
   165→// enough to produce a valid evaluation scope. If the returned plan is nil
   166→// then the scope will always be nil, but it's also possible for the scope
   167→// to be nil even when the plan isn't, if the plan is not complete enough for
   168→//

   412→func (c *Context) plan(config *configs.Config, prevRunState *states.State, opts *PlanOpts) (*plans.Plan, *lang.Scope, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {
   413→	var diags tfdiags.Diagnostics
   414→	if opts.Mode != plans.NormalMode {
   415→		panic(fmt.Sprintf("called Context.plan with %s", opts.Mode))
   416→	}
   417→
   418→	plan, evalScope, walkDiags := c.planWalk(config, prevRunState, opts)
   419→	diags = diags.Append(walkDiags)
   420→
   421→	return plan, evalScope, diags
   422→}
   423→
   424→func (c *Context) refreshOnlyPlan(config *configs.Config, prevRunState *states.State, opts *PlanOpts) (*plans.Plan, *lang.Scope, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {

   426→
   427→	if opts.Mode != plans.RefreshOnlyMode {
   428→		panic(fmt.Sprintf("called Context.refreshOnlyPlan with %s", opts.Mode))
   429→	}

   432→	diags = diags.Append(walkDiags)
   433→	if diags.HasErrors() {
   434→		// Non-nil plan along with errors indicates a non-applyable partial
   435→		// plan that's only suitable to be shown to the user as extra context
   436→		// to help understand the errors.
   437→		return plan, evalScope, diags

   552→
   553→func (c *Context) prePlanFindAndApplyMoves(config *configs.Config, prevRunState *states.State) ([]refactoring.MoveStatement, refactoring.MoveResults, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {
   554→	explicitMoveStmts := refactoring.FindMoveStatements(config)
   555→	implicitMoveStmts := refactoring.ImpliedMoveStatements(config, prevRunState, explicitMoveStmts)
   556→	var moveStmts []refactoring.MoveStatement
   557→	if stmtsLen := len(explicitMoveStmts) + len(implicitMoveStmts); stmtsLen > 0 {
   558→		moveStmts = make([]refactoring.MoveStatement, 0, stmtsLen)
   559→		moveStmts = append(moveStmts, explicitMoveStmts...)
   560→		moveStmts = append(moveStmts, implicitMoveStmts...)
   561→	}
   562→	moveResults, diags := refactoring.ApplyMoves(moveStmts, prevRunState, c.plugins.ProviderFactories())
   563→	return moveStmts, moveResults, diags
   564→}
   565→
   566→func (c *Context) prePlanVerifyTargetedMoves(moveResults refactoring.MoveResults, targets []addrs.Targetable) tfdiags.Diagnostics {
   567→	if len(targets) < 1 {
   568→		return nil // the following only matters when targeting
   569→	}
   570→
   571→	var diags tfdiags.Diagnostics
   572→
   573→	var excluded []addrs.AbsResourceInstance
   574→	for _, result := range moveResults.Changes.Values() {
   575→		fromMatchesTarget := false
   576→		toMatchesTarget := false
   577→		for _, targetAddr := range targets {
   578→			if targetAddr.TargetContains(result.From) {

    17→func buildProviderConfig(ctx EvalContext, addr addrs.AbsProviderConfig, config *configs.Provider) hcl.Body {
    18→	var configBody hcl.Body
    19→	if config != nil {
    20→		configBody = config.Config
    21→	}
    22→
    23→	var inputBody hcl.Body
    24→	inputConfig := ctx.ProviderInput(addr)
    25→	if len(inputConfig) > 0 {
    26→		inputBody = configs.SynthBody("<input-prompt>", inputConfig)
    27→	}
    28→
    29→	switch {
    30→	case configBody != nil && inputBody != nil:
    31→		log.Printf("[TRACE] buildProviderConfig for %s: merging explicit config and input", addr)
    32→		return hcl.MergeBodies([]hcl.Body{inputBody, configBody})
    33→	case configBody != nil:
    34→		log.Printf("[TRACE] buildProviderConfig for %s: using explicit config only", addr)
    35→		return configBody
    36→	case inputBody != nil:
    37→		log.Printf("[TRACE] buildProviderConfig for %s: using input only", addr)
    38→		return inputBody
    39→	default:
    40→		log.Printf("[TRACE] buildProviderConfig for %s: no configuration at all", addr)
    41→		return hcl.EmptyBody()
    42→	}
    43→}

   138→func (ctx *BuiltinEvalContext) InitProvider(addr addrs.AbsProviderConfig, config *configs.Provider) (providers.Interface, error) {
   139→	// If we already initialized, it is an error
   140→	if p := ctx.Provider(addr); p != nil {
   141→		return nil, fmt.Errorf("%s is already initialized", addr)
   142→	}
   143→
   144→	// Warning: make sure to acquire these locks AFTER the call to Provider
   145→	// above, since it also acquires locks.
   146→	ctx.ProviderLock.Lock()
   147→	defer ctx.ProviderLock.Unlock()
   148→
   149→	key := addr.String()
   150→
   151→	if addr.Module.IsRoot() {
   152→		rootAddr := addrs.RootProviderConfig{
   153→			Provider: addr.Provider,
   154→			Alias:    addr.Alias,
   155→		}
   156→		if external, isExternal := ctx.ExternalProviderConfigs[rootAddr]; isExternal {
   157→			// External providers should always be pre-configured by the
   158→			// external caller, and so we'll wrap them in a type that
   159→			// makes operations like ConfigureProvider and Close be no-op.
   160→			wrapped := externalProviderWrapper{external}

   257→func (t *CloseProviderTransformer) Transform(g *Graph) error {
   258→	pm := providerVertexMap(g)
   259→	cpm := make(map[string]*graphNodeCloseProvider)
   260→	var err error
   261→
   262→	for _, p := range pm {
   263→		key := p.ProviderAddr().String()
   264→
   265→		// make sure we haven't created the closer node already
   266→		_, ok := cpm[key]
   267→		if ok {
   268→			log.Printf("[ERROR] CloseProviderTransformer: already created close node for %s", key)
   269→			continue
   270→		}
   271→
   272→		// create a closer for this provider type
   273→		closer := &graphNodeCloseProvider{Addr: p.ProviderAddr()}
   274→		g.Add(closer)
   275→		cpm[key] = closer
   276→
   277→		// Close node depends on the provider itself
   278→		// this is added unconditionally, so it will connect to all instances
   279→		// of the provider. Extra edges will be removed by transitive
   280→		// reduction.
   281→		g.Connect(dag.BasicEdge(closer, p))
   282→	}
   283→
   284→	// Now look for all provider consumers and connect them to the appropriate closers.
   285→	for _, v := range g.Vertices() {
   286→		pc, ok := v.(GraphNodeProviderConsumer)
   287→		if !ok {
   288→			continue
   289→		}
   290→
   291→		p, exact := pc.ProvidedBy()
   292→		if p == nil && exact {
   293→			// this node does not require a provider
   294→			continue
   295→		}
   296→
   297→		provider, ok := p.(addrs.AbsProviderConfig)

This command will not\n  actually perform the planned actions.\n\n  You can optionally save the plan to a file, which you can then pass to\n  the \"apply\" command to perform exactly the actions described in the plan.\n\nPlan Customization Options:\n\n  The following options customize how Terraform will produce its plan. You can use\n                      this option multiple times to replace more than one object.\n\n  -target=resource    Limit the planning operation to only the given module,\n                      resource, or resource instance and all of its\n                      dependencies. This is for exceptional\n                      use only.\n\n  -var 'foo=bar'      Set a value for one of the input variables in the root\n                      module of the configuration. len(opts.SetVariables))\n\tapplyTimeVariables := collections.NewSetCmp[string]()\n\tfor k, iv := range opts.SetVariables {\n\t\t// If any input variables were declared as ephemeral and set to a\n\t\t// non-null value then those variables must be provided again (possibly\n\t\t// with _different_ non-null values) during the apply phase.\n\t\tif vc, ok := config.Module.Variables[k]; ok && vc.Ephemeral {\n\t\t\t// FIXME: We should actually do this based on the final value\n\t\t\t// in the named values state, rather than the value as provided\n\t\t\t// by the caller, so we can take into account the transforms\n\t\t\t// done during variable evaluation. This is a plausible starting\n\t\t\t// point for now, though.\n\t\t\tif iv.Value != cty.NilVal && !iv.Value.IsNull() {\n\t\t\t\tapplyTimeVariables.Add(k)\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t}\n\n\t\t// Non-ephemeral variables must remain unchanged between plan and\n\t\t// apply, so we'll record their actual values.\n\t\tif iv.Value == cty.NilVal {\n\t\t\tcontinue // We only record values that the caller actually set\n\t\t}\n\n\t\t// Root variable values arriving from the traditional CLI path are\n\t\t// unmarked, as they are directly decoded from .tfvars, CLI arguments,\n\t\t// or the environment. However, variable values arriving from other\n\t\t// plans (via the coordination efforts of the stacks runtime) may have\n\t\t// gathered marks during evaluation. We must separate the value from\n\t\t// its marks here to maintain compatibility with plans.DynamicValue,\n\t\t// which cannot represent marks.\n\t\tvalue, pvm := iv.Value.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\n\n\t\t// We use cty.DynamicPseudoType here so that we'll save both the\n\t\t// value _and_ its dynamic type in the plan, so we can recover\n\t\t// exactly the same value later.\n\t\tdv, err := plans.NewDynamicValue(value, cty.DynamicPseudoType)\n\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(tfdiags.Sourceless(\n\t\t\t\ttfdiags.Error,\n\t\t\t\t\"Failed to prepare variable value for plan\",\n\t\t\t\tfmt.Sprintf(\"The value for variable %q could not be serialized to store in the plan: %s.\", k, err),\n\t\t\t))\n\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t}\n\t\tvarVals[k] = dv\n\t\tvarMarks[k] = pvm\n\t}\n\n\t// insert the run-specific data from the context into the plan; variables,\n\t// targets and provider SHAs.\n\tif plan != nil {\n\t\tplan.VariableValues = varVals\n\t\tplan.ApplyTimeVariables = applyTimeVariables\n\t\tif len(varMarks) > 0 {\n\t\t\tplan.VariableMarks = varMarks\n\t\t}\n\t\tplan.TargetAddrs = opts.Targets\n\t} else if !diags.HasErrors() {\n\t\tpanic(\"nil plan but no errors\")\n\t}\n\n\tif plan != nil {\n\t\trelevantAttrs, rDiags := c.relevantResourceAttrsForPlan(config, plan)\n\t\tdiags = diags.Append(rDiags)\n\t\tplan.RelevantAttributes = relevantAttrs\n\t}\n\n\tif diags.HasErrors() {\n\t\t// We can't proceed further with an invalid plan, because an invalid\n\t\t// plan isn't applyable by definition.\n\t\tif plan != nil {\n\t\t\t// We'll explicitly mark our plan as errored so that it can't\n\t\t\t// be accidentally applied even though it's incomplete.\n\t\t\tplan.Errored = true\n\t\t}\n\t\treturn plan, evalScope, diags\n\t}\n\n\tdiags = diags.Append(c.checkApplyGraph(plan, config, opts))\n\n\treturn plan, evalScope, diags\n}\n\n// checkApplyGraph builds the apply graph out of the current plan to\n// check for any errors that may arise once the planned changes are added to\n// the graph. This allows terraform to report errors (mostly cycles) during\n// plan that would otherwise only crop up during apply\nfunc (c *Context) checkApplyGraph(plan *plans.Plan, config *configs.Config, opts *PlanOpts) tfdiags.Diagnostics {\n\tif plan.Changes.Empty() {\n\t\tlog.Println(\"[DEBUG] no planned changes, skipping apply graph check\")\n\t\treturn nil\n\t}\n\tlog.Println(\"[DEBUG] building apply graph to check for errors\")\n\n\t_, _, diags := c.applyGraph(plan, config, opts.ApplyOpts(), true)\n\treturn diags\n}\n\nvar DefaultPlanOpts = &PlanOpts{\n\tMode: plans.NormalMode,\n}\n\n// SimplePlanOpts is a constructor to help with creating \"simple\" values of\n// PlanOpts which only specify a mode and input variables.\n//\n// This helper function is primarily intended for use in straightforward\n// tests that don't need any of the more \"esoteric\" planning options. For\n// handling real user requests to run Terraform, it'd probably be better\n// to construct a *PlanOpts value directly and provide a way for the user\n// to set values for all of its fields.\n//\n// The \"mode\" and \"setVariables\" arguments become the values of the \"Mode\"\n// and \"SetVariables\" fields in the result. Refer to the PlanOpts type\n// documentation to learn about the meanings of those fields.\nfunc SimplePlanOpts(mode plans.Mode, setVariables InputValues) *PlanOpts {\n\treturn &PlanOpts{\n\t\tMode:         mode,\n\t\tSetVariables: setVariables,\n\t}\n}\n\nfunc (c *Context) plan(config *configs.Config, prevRunState *states.State, opts *PlanOpts) (*plans.Plan, *lang.Scope, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n\tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n\tif opts.Mode != plans.NormalMode {\n\t\tpanic(fmt.Sprintf(\"called Context.plan with %s\", opts.Mode))\n\t}\n\n\tplan, evalScope, walkDiags := c.planWalk(config, prevRunState, opts)\n\tdiags = diags.Append(walkDiags)\n\n\treturn plan, evalScope, diags\n}\n\nfunc (c *Context) refreshOnlyPlan(config *configs.Config, prevRunState *states.State, opts *PlanOpts) (*plans.Plan, *lang.Scope, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n\tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n\n\tif opts.Mode != plans.RefreshOnlyMode {\n\t\tpanic(fmt.Sprintf(\"called Context.refreshOnlyPlan with %s\", opts.Mode))\n\t}\n\n\tplan, evalScope, walkDiags := c.planWalk(config, prevRunState, opts)\n\tdiags = diags.Append(walkDiags)\n\tif diags.HasErrors() {\n\t\t// Non-nil plan along with errors indicates a non-applyable partial\n\t\t// plan that's only suitable to be shown to the user as extra context\n\t\t// to help understand the errors.\n\t\treturn plan, evalScope, diags\n\t}\n\n\t// If the graph builder and graph nodes correctly obeyed our directive\n\t// to refresh only, the set of resource changes should always be empty.\n\t// We'll safety-check that here so we can return a clear message about it,\n\t// rather than probably just generating confusing output at the UI layer.\n\tif len(plan.Changes.Resources) != 0 {\n\t\t// Some extra context in the logs in case the user reports this message\n\t\t// as a bug, as a starting point for debugging.\n\t\tfor _, rc := range plan.Changes.Resources {\n\t\t\tif depKey := rc.DeposedKey; depKey == states.NotDeposed {\n\t\t\t\tlog.Printf(\"[DEBUG] Refresh-only plan includes %s change for %s\", rc.Action, rc.Addr)\n\t\t\t} else {\n\t\t\t\tlog.Printf(\"[DEBUG] Refresh-only plan includes %s change for %s deposed object %s\", rc.Action, rc.Addr, depKey)\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\t\tdiags = diags.Append(tfdiags.Sourceless(\n\t\t\ttfdiags.Error,\n\t\t\t\"Invalid refresh-only plan\",\n\t\t\t\"Terraform generated planned resource changes in a refresh-only plan. This is a bug in Terraform.\",\n\t\t))\n\t}\n\n\t// We don't populate RelevantResources for a refresh-only plan, because\n\t// they never have any planned actions and so no resource can ever be\n\t// \"relevant\" per the intended meaning of that field.\n\n\treturn plan, evalScope, diags\n}\n\nfunc (c *Context) destroyPlan(config *configs.Config, prevRunState *states.State, opts *PlanOpts) (*plans.Plan, *lang.Scope, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n\tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n\n\tif opts.Mode != plans.DestroyMode {\n\t\tpanic(fmt.Sprintf(\"called Context.destroyPlan with %s\", opts.Mode))\n\t}\n\n\tpriorState := prevRunState\n\n\t// A destroy plan starts by running Refresh to read any pending data\n\t// sources, and remove missing managed resources. This is required because\n\t// a \"destroy plan\" is only creating delete changes, and is essentially a\n\t// local operation.\n\t//\n\t// NOTE: if skipRefresh _is_ set then we'll rely on the destroy-plan walk\n\t// below to upgrade the prevRunState and priorState both to the latest\n\t// resource type schemas, so NodePlanDestroyableResourceInstance.Execute\n\t// must coordinate with this by taking that action only when c.skipRefresh\n\t// _is_ set. This coupling between the two is unfortunate but necessary\n\t// to work within our current structure.\n\tif !opts.SkipRefresh && !prevRunState.Empty() {\n\t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] Context.destroyPlan: calling Context.plan to get the effect of refreshing the prior state\")\n\t\trefreshOpts := *opts\n\t\trefreshOpts.Mode = plans.NormalMode\n\t\trefreshOpts.PreDestroyRefresh = true\n\n\t\t// FIXME: A normal plan is required here to refresh the state, because\n\t\t// the state and configuration may not match during a destroy, and a\n\t\t// normal refresh plan can fail with evaluation errors. In the future\n\t\t// the destroy plan should take care of refreshing instances itself,\n\t\t// where the special cases of evaluation and skipping condition checks\n\t\t// can be done.\n\t\trefreshPlan, _, refreshDiags := c.plan(config, prevRunState, &refreshOpts)\n\t\tif refreshDiags.HasErrors() {\n\t\t\t// NOTE: Normally we'd append diagnostics regardless of whether\n\t\t\t// there are errors, just in case there are warnings we'd want to\n\t\t\t// preserve, but we're intentionally _not_ doing that here because\n\t\t\t// if the first plan succeeded then we'll be running another plan\n\t\t\t// in DestroyMode below, and we don't want to double-up any\n\t\t\t// warnings that both plan walks would generate.\n\t\t\t// (This does mean we won't show any warnings that would've been\n\t\t\t// unique to only this walk, but we're assuming here that if the\n\t\t\t// warnings aren't also applicable to a destroy plan then we'd\n\t\t\t// rather not show them here, because this non-destroy plan for\n\t\t\t// refreshing is largely an implementation detail.)\n\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(refreshDiags)\n\t\t\treturn nil, nil, diags\n\t\t}\n\n\t\t// We'll use the refreshed state -- which is the  \"prior state\" from\n\t\t// the perspective of this \"destroy plan\" -- as the starting state\n\t\t// for our destroy-plan walk, so it can take into account if we\n\t\t// detected during refreshing that anything was already deleted outside\n\t\t// of Terraform.\n\t\tpriorState = refreshPlan.PriorState.DeepCopy()\n\n\t\t// The refresh plan may have upgraded state for some resources, make\n\t\t// sure we store the new version.\n\t\tprevRunState = refreshPlan.PrevRunState.DeepCopy()\n\t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] Context.destroyPlan: now _really_ creating a destroy plan\")\n\t}\n\n\tdestroyPlan, evalScope, walkDiags := c.planWalk(config, priorState, opts)\n\tdiags = diags.Append(walkDiags)\n\tif walkDiags.HasErrors() {\n\t\t// Non-nil plan along with errors indicates a non-applyable partial\n\t\t// plan that's only suitable to be shown to the user as extra context\n\t\t// to help understand the errors.\n\t\treturn destroyPlan, evalScope, diags\n\t}\n\n\tif !opts.SkipRefresh {\n\t\t// If we didn't skip refreshing then we want the previous run state to\n\t\t// be the one we originally fed into the c.refreshOnlyPlan call above,\n\t\t// not the refreshed version we used for the destroy planWalk.\n\t\tdestroyPlan.PrevRunState = prevRunState\n\t}\n\n\trelevantAttrs, rDiags := c.relevantResourceAttrsForPlan(config, destroyPlan)\n\tdiags = diags.Append(rDiags)\n\n\tdestroyPlan.RelevantAttributes = relevantAttrs\n\treturn destroyPlan, evalScope, diags\n}\n\nfunc (c *Context) prePlanFindAndApplyMoves(config *configs.Config, prevRunState *states.State) ([]refactoring.MoveStatement, refactoring.MoveResults, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n\texplicitMoveStmts := refactoring.FindMoveStatements(config)\n\timplicitMoveStmts := refactoring.ImpliedMoveStatements(config, prevRunState, explicitMoveStmts)\n\tvar moveStmts []refactoring.MoveStatement\n\tif stmtsLen := len(explicitMoveStmts) + len(implicitMoveStmts); stmtsLen > 0 {\n\t\tmoveStmts = make([]refactoring.MoveStatement, 0, stmtsLen)\n\t\tmoveStmts = append(moveStmts, explicitMoveStmts...)\n\t\tmoveStmts = append(moveStmts, implicitMoveStmts...)\n\t}\n\tmoveResults, diags := refactoring.ApplyMoves(moveStmts, prevRunState, c.plugins.ProviderFactories())\n\treturn moveStmts, moveResults, diags\n}\n\nfunc (c *Context) prePlanVerifyTargetedMoves(moveResults refactoring.MoveResults, targets []addrs.Targetable) tfdiags.Diagnostics {\n\tif len(targets) < 1 {\n\t\treturn nil // the following only matters when targeting\n\t}\n\n\tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n\n\tvar excluded []addrs.AbsResourceInstance\n\tfor _, result := range moveResults.Changes.Values() {\n\t\tfromMatchesTarget := false\n\t\ttoMatchesTarget := false\n\t\tfor _, targetAddr := range targets {\n\t\t\tif targetAddr.TargetContains(result.From) {\n\t\t\t\tfromMatchesTarget = true\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tif targetAddr.TargetContains(result.To) {\n\t\t\t\ttoMatchesTarget = true\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\t\tif !fromMatchesTarget {\n\t\t\texcluded = append(excluded, result.From)\n\t\t}\n\t\tif !toMatchesTarget {\n\t\t\texcluded = append(excluded, result.To)\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\tif len(excluded) > 0 {\n\t\tsort.Slice(excluded, func(i, j int) bool {\n\t\t\treturn excluded[i].Less(excluded[j])\n\t\t})\n\n\t\tvar listBuf strings.Builder\n\t\tvar prevResourceAddr addrs.AbsResource\n\t\tfor _, instAddr := range excluded {\n\t\t\t// Targeting generally ends up selecting whole resources rather\n\t\t\t// than individual instances, because we don't factor in\n\t\t\t// individual instances until DynamicExpand, so we're going to\n\t\t\t// always show whole resource addresses here, excluding any\n\t\t\t// instance keys. (This also neatly avoids dealing with the\n\t\t\t// different quoting styles required for string instance keys\n\t\t\t// on different shells, which is handy.)\n\t\t\t//\n\t\t\t// To avoid showing duplicates when we have multiple instances\n\t\t\t// of the same resource, we'll remember the most recent\n\t\t\t// resource we rendered in prevResource, which is sufficient\n\t\t\t// because we sorted the list of instance addresses above, and\n\t\t\t// our sort order always groups together instances of the same\n\t\t\t// resource.\n\t\t\tresourceAddr := instAddr.ContainingResource()\n\t\t\tif resourceAddr.Equal(prevResourceAddr) {\n\t\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tfmt.Fprintf(&listBuf, \"\\n  -target=%q\", resourceAddr.String())\n\t\t\tprevResourceAddr = resourceAddr\n\t\t}\n\t\tdiags = diags.Append(tfdiags.Sourceless(\n\t\t\ttfdiags.Error,\n\t\t\t\"Moved resource instances excluded by targeting\",\n\t\t\tfmt.Sprintf(\n\t\t\t\t\"Resource instances in your current state have moved to new addresses in the latest configuration. Terraform must include those resource instances while planning in order to ensure a correct result, but your -target=... options do not fully cover all of those resource instances.\\n\\nTo create a valid plan, either remove your -target=... options altogether or add the following additional target options:%s\\n\\nNote that adding these options may include further additional resource instances in your plan, in order to respect object dependencies.\",\n\t\t\t\tlistBuf.String(),\n\t\t\t),\n\t\t))\n\t}\n\n\treturn diags\n}\n\nfunc (c *Context) postPlanValidateMoves(config *configs.Config, stmts []refactoring.MoveStatement, allInsts instances.Set) tfdiags.Diagnostics {\n\treturn refactoring.ValidateMoves(stmts, config, allInsts)\n}\n\n// findImportTargets builds a list of import targets from any import blocks in\n// config.\nfunc (c *Context) findImportTargets(config *configs.Config) []*ImportTarget {\n\tvar importTargets []*ImportTarget\n\tfor _, ic := range config.Module.Import {\n\t\timportTargets = append(importTargets, &ImportTarget{\n\t\t\tConfig: ic,\n\t\t})\n\t}\n\treturn importTargets\n}\n\n// findForgetTargets builds a list of resources and a list of modules to be\n// forgotten, based on any removed blocks in config.\nfunc (c *Context) findForgetTargets(config *configs.Config) (forgetResources []addrs.ConfigResource, forgetModules []addrs.Module, diags tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n\tremoveStmts, diags := refactoring.FindRemoveStatements(config)\n\tif diags.HasErrors() {\n\t\treturn nil, nil, diags\n\t}\n\tfor _, rst := range removeStmts.Values() {\n\t\tif rst.Destroy {\n\t\t\t// no-op\n\t\t} else {\n\t\t\tif fr, ok := rst.From.(addrs.ConfigResource); ok {\n\t\t\t\tforgetResources = append(forgetResources, fr)\n\t\t\t} else if fm, ok := rst.From.(addrs.Module); ok {\n\t\t\t\tforgetModules = append(forgetModules, fm)\n\t\t\t} else {\n\t\t\t\tpanic(\"Invalid ConfigMoveable type in remove statement\")\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\treturn forgetResources, forgetModules, diags\n}\n\nfunc (c *Context) planWalk(config *configs.Config, prevRunState *states.State, opts *PlanOpts) (*plans.Plan, *lang.Scope, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n\tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n\tlog.Printf(\"[DEBUG] Building and walking plan graph for %s\", opts.Mode)\n\n\tprevRunState = prevRunState.DeepCopy() // don't modify the caller's object when we process the moves\n\tmoveStmts, moveResults, moveDiags := c.prePlanFindAndApplyMoves(config, prevRunState)\n\tdiags = diags.Append(moveDiags)\n\tif moveDiags.HasErrors() {\n\t\treturn nil, nil, diags\n\t}\n\n\t// If resource targeting is in effect then it might conflict with the\n\t// move result.\n\tdiags = diags.Append(c.prePlanVerifyTargetedMoves(moveResults, opts.Targets))\n\tif diags.HasErrors() {\n\t\t// We'll return early here, because if we have any moved resource\n\t\t// instances excluded by targeting then planning is likely to encounter\n\t\t// strange problems that may lead to confusing error messages.\n\t\treturn nil, nil, diags\n\t}\n\n\tgraph, walkOp, moreDiags := c.planGraph(config, prevRunState, opts)\n\tdiags = diags.Append(moreDiags)\n\tif diags.HasErrors() {\n\t\treturn nil, nil, diags\n\t}\n\n\ttimestamp := time.Now().UTC()\n\tif opts.ForcePlanTimestamp != nil {\n\t\t// Some tests use this to produce stable results to assert against.\n\t\ttimestamp = *opts.ForcePlanTimestamp\n\t}\n\n\tvar externalProviderConfigs map[addrs.RootProviderConfig]providers.Interface\n\tif opts != nil {\n\t\texternalProviderConfigs = opts.ExternalProviders\n\t}\n\n\t// If we get here then we should definitely have a non-nil \"graph\", which\n\t// we can now walk.\n\tchanges := plans.NewChanges()\n\n\t// Initialize the results table to validate provider function calls.\n\t// Hold reference to this so we can store the table data in the plan file.\n\tproviderFuncResults := providers.NewFunctionResultsTable(nil)\n\n\twalker, walkDiags := c.walk(graph, walkOp, &graphWalkOpts{\n\t\tConfig:                     config,\n\t\tInputState:                 prevRunState,\n\t\tExternalProviderConfigs:    externalProviderConfigs,\n\t\tDeferralAllowed:            opts.DeferralAllowed,\n\t\tExternalDependencyDeferred: opts.ExternalDependencyDeferred,\n\t\tChanges:                    changes,\n\t\tMoveResults:                moveResults,\n\t\tOverrides:                  opts.Overrides,\n\t\tPlanTimeTimestamp:          timestamp,\n\t\tProviderFuncResults:        providerFuncResults,\n\t\tForget:                     opts.Forget,\n\t})\n\tdiags = diags.Append(walker.NonFatalDiagnostics)\n\tdiags = diags.Append(walkDiags)\n\n\tallInsts := walker.InstanceExpander.AllInstances()\n\n\tmoveValidateDiags := c.postPlanValidateMoves(config, moveStmts, allInsts)\n\tif moveValidateDiags.HasErrors() {\n\t\t// If any of the move statements are invalid then those errors take\n\t\t// precedence over any other errors because an incomplete move graph\n\t\t// is quite likely to be the _cause_ of various errors. This oddity\n\t\t// comes from the fact that we need to apply the moves before we\n\t\t// actually validate them, because validation depends on the result\n\t\t// of first trying to plan.\n\t\treturn nil, nil, moveValidateDiags\n\t}\n\tdiags = diags.Append(moveValidateDiags) // might just contain warnings\n\n\tif moveResults.Blocked.Len() > 0 && !diags.HasErrors() {\n\t\t// If we had blocked moves and we're not going to be returning errors\n\t\t// then we'll report the blockers as a warning. We do this only in the\n\t\t// absense of errors because invalid move statements might well be\n\t\t// the root cause of the blockers, and so better to give an actionable\n\t\t// error message than a less-actionable warning.\n\t\tdiags = diags.Append(blockedMovesWarningDiag(moveResults))\n\t}\n\n\t// If we reach this point with error diagnostics then \"changes\" is a\n\t// representation of the subset of changes we were able to plan before\n\t// we encountered errors, which we'll return as part of a non-nil plan\n\t// so that e.g. the UI can show what was planned so far in case that extra\n\t// context helps the user to understand the error messages we're returning.\n\tprevRunState = walker.PrevRunState.Close()\n\n\t// The refreshed state may have data resource objects which were deferred\n\t// to apply and cannot be serialized.\n\twalker.RefreshState.RemovePlannedResourceInstanceObjects()\n\tpriorState := walker.RefreshState.Close()\n\n\tdriftedResources, driftDiags := c.driftedResources(config, prevRunState, priorState, moveResults)\n\tdiags = diags.Append(driftDiags)\n\n\tdeferredResources, deferredDiags := c.deferredResources(config, walker.Deferrals.GetDeferredChanges(), priorState)\n\tdiags = diags.Append(deferredDiags)\n\n\tvar forgottenResources []string\n\tfor _, rc := range changes.Resources {\n\t\tif rc.Action == plans.Forget {\n\t\t\t// TODO KEM display resource ids\n\t\t\tforgottenResources = append(forgottenResources, fmt.Sprintf(\" - %s\", rc.Addr))\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\tif len(forgottenResources) > 0 {\n\t\tdiags = diags.Append(tfdiags.Sourceless(\n\t\t\ttfdiags.Warning,\n\t\t\t\"Some objects will no longer be managed by Terraform\",\n\t\t\tfmt.Sprintf(\"If you apply this plan, Terraform will discard its tracking information for the following objects, but it will not delete them:\\n%s\\n\\nAfter applying this plan, Terraform will no longer manage these objects. You will need to import them into Terraform to manage them again.\", strings.Join(forgottenResources, \"\\n\")),\n\t\t))\n\t}\n\tschemas, schemaDiags := c.Schemas(config, prevRunState)\n\t// We must finish building a plan object, and cannot return early here.\n\tvar changesSrc *plans.ChangesSrc\n\tvar err error\n\tif !schemaDiags.HasErrors() {\n\t\tchangesSrc, err = changes.Encode(schemas)\n\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(err)\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\tplan := &plans.Plan{\n\t\tUIMode:                  opts.Mode,\n\t\tChanges:                 changesSrc,\n\t\tDriftedResources:        driftedResources,\n\t\tDeferredResources:       deferredResources,\n\t\tPrevRunState:            prevRunState,\n\t\tPriorState:              priorState,\n\t\tExternalReferences:      opts.ExternalReferences,\n\t\tOverrides:               opts.Overrides,\n\t\tChecks:                  states.NewCheckResults(walker.Checks),\n\t\tTimestamp:               timestamp,\n\t\tProviderFunctionResults: providerFuncResults.GetHashes(),\n\n\t\t// Other fields get populated by Context.Plan after we return\n\t}\n\n\t// Our final rulings on whether the plan is \"complete\" and \"applyable\".\n\t// See the documentation for these plan fields to learn what exactly they\n\t// are intended to mean.\n\tif !diags.HasErrors() {\n\t\tif len(opts.Targets) == 0 && !walker.Deferrals.HaveAnyDeferrals() {\n\t\t\t// A plan without any targets or deferred actions should be\n\t\t\t// complete if we didn't encounter errors while producing it.\n\t\t\tlog.Println(\"[TRACE] Plan is complete\")\n\t\t\tplan.Complete = true\n\t\t} else {\n\t\t\tlog.Println(\"[TRACE] Plan is incomplete\")\n\t\t}\n\t\tif opts.Mode == plans.RefreshOnlyMode {\n\t\t\t// In refresh-only mode we explicitly don't expect to propose any\n\t\t\t// actions, but the plan is applyable if the state was changed\n\t\t\t// in an interesting way by the refresh step.\n\t\t\tplan.Applyable = !plan.PriorState.ManagedResourcesEqual(plan.PrevRunState) || !plan.PriorState.RootOutputValuesEqual(plan.PrevRunState)\n\t\t} else {\n\t\t\t// For other planning modes a plan is applyable if its \"changes\"\n\t\t\t// are not considered empty (by whatever rules the plans package\n\t\t\t// uses to decide that).\n\t\t\tplan.Applyable = !plan.Changes.Empty()\n\t\t}\n\t\tif plan.Applyable {\n\t\t\tlog.Println(\"[TRACE] Plan is applyable\")\n\t\t} else {\n\t\t\tlog.Println(\"[TRACE] Plan is not applyable\")\n\t\t}\n\t} else {\n\t\tlog.Println(\"[WARN] Planning encountered errors, so plan is not applyable\")\n\t}\n\n\t// The caller also gets access to an expression evaluation scope in the\n\t// root module, in case it needs to extract other information using\n\t// expressions, like in \"terraform console\" or the test harness.\n\tevalScope := evalScopeFromGraphWalk(walker, addrs.RootModuleInstance)\n\n\treturn plan, evalScope, diags\n}\n\nfunc (c *Context) deferredResources(config *configs.Config, deferrals []*plans.DeferredResourceInstanceChange, state *states.State) This is known to happen when targeting a subset of resources,\n// because the excluded instances will have been removed from the plan and\n// not upgraded.\nfunc (c *Context) driftedResources(config *configs.Config, oldState, newState *states.State, moves refactoring.MoveResults) ([]*plans.ResourceInstanceChangeSrc, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n\tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n\n\tif newState.ManagedResourcesEqual(oldState) && moves.Changes.Len() == 0 {\n\t\t// Nothing to do, because we only detect and report drift for managed\n\t\t// resource instances.\n\t\treturn nil, {\n\t\t\t\t\tnewObj, err = newIS.Current.Decode(ty)\n\t\t\t\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\t\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(tfdiags.Sourceless(\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\ttfdiags.Warning,\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\"Failed to decode resource from state\",\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\tfmt.Sprintf(\"Error decoding %q from prior state: %s\", addr.String(), err),\n\t\t\t\t\t\t))\n\t\t\t\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t\t}\n\n\t\t\t\tvar oldVal, oldVal.RawEquals(newVal) && addr.Equal(prevRunAddr) {\n\t\t\t\t\t// No drift if the two values are semantically equivalent\n\t\t\t\t\t// and no move has happened\n\t\t\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t\t\t}\n\n\t\t\t\t// We can detect three types of changes after refreshing state,\n\t\t\t\t// only two of which are easily understood as \"drift\":\n\t\t\t\t//\n\t\t\t\t// - Resources which were deleted outside of Terraform;\n\t\t\t\t// - Resources where the object value has changed outside of\n\t\t\t\t//   Terraform;\n\t\t\t\t// - This is a bug in Terraform.\",\n   458\u2192\t\t))\n   459\u2192\t}\n   460\u2192\n   461\u2192\t// We don't populate RelevantResources for a refresh-only plan, because\n   462\u2192\t// they never have any planned actions and so no resource can ever be\n   463\u2192\t// \"relevant\" per the intended meaning of that field.\n   464\u2192\n   465\u2192\treturn plan, evalScope, diags\n   466\u2192}\n   467\u2192\n   468\u2192func (c *Context) destroyPlan(config *configs.Config, prevRunState *states.State, opts *PlanOpts) (*plans.Plan, *lang.Scope, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n   469\u2192\tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n   470\u2192\n   471\u2192\tif opts.Mode != plans.DestroyMode {\n   472\u2192\t\tpanic(fmt.Sprintf(\"called Context.destroyPlan with %s\", opts.Mode))\n   473\u2192\t}\n   474\u2192\n   475\u2192\tpriorState := prevRunState\n   476\u2192\n   477\u2192\t// A destroy plan starts by running Refresh to read any pending data\n   478\u2192\t// sources, and remove missing managed resources. This is required because\n   479\u2192\t// a \"destroy plan\" is only creating delete changes, and is essentially a\n   480\u2192\t// local operation.\n   481\u2192\t//\n   482\u2192\t// NOTE: if skipRefresh _is_ set then we'll rely on the destroy-plan walk\n   483\u2192\t// below to upgrade the prevRunState and priorState both to the latest\n   484\u2192\t// resource type schemas, so NodePlanDestroyableResourceInstance.Execute\n   485\u2192\t// must coordinate with this by taking that action only when c.skipRefresh\n   486\u2192\t// _is_ set. This coupling between the two is unfortunate but necessary\n   487\u2192\t// to work within our current structure.\n   488\u2192\tif !opts.SkipRefresh && !prevRunState.Empty() {\n   489\u2192\t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] Context.destroyPlan: calling Context.plan to get the effect of refreshing the prior state\")\n   490\u2192\t\trefreshOpts := *opts\n   491\u2192\t\trefreshOpts.Mode = plans.NormalMode\n   492\u2192\t\trefreshOpts.PreDestroyRefresh = true\n   493\u2192\n   494\u2192\t\t// FIXME: A normal plan is required here to refresh the state, because\n   495\u2192\t\t// the state and configuration may not match during a destroy, and a\n   496\u2192\t\t// normal refresh plan can fail with evaluation errors. In the future\n   497\u2192\t\t// the destroy plan should take care of refreshing instances itself,\n   498\u2192\t\t// where the special cases of evaluation and skipping condition checks\n   499\u2192\t\t// can be done.\n   500\u2192\t\trefreshPlan, _, refreshDiags := c.plan(config, prevRunState, &refreshOpts)\n   501\u2192\t\tif refreshDiags.HasErrors() {\n   502\u2192\t\t\t// NOTE: Normally we'd append diagnostics regardless of whether\n   503\u2192\t\t\t// there are errors, just in case there are warnings we'd want to\n   504\u2192\t\t\t// preserve, but we're intentionally _not_ doing that here because\n   505\u2192\t\t\t// if the first plan succeeded then we'll be running another plan\n   506\u2192\t\t\t// in DestroyMode below, and we don't want to double-up any\n   507\u2192\t\t\t// warnings that both plan walks would generate.\n   508\u2192\t\t\t// (This does mean we won't show any warnings that would've been\n   509\u2192\t\t\t// unique to only this walk, but we're assuming here that if the\n   510\u2192\t\t\t// warnings aren't also applicable to a destroy plan then we'd\n   511\u2192\t\t\t// rather not show them here, because this non-destroy plan for\n   512\u2192\t\t\t// refreshing is largely an implementation detail.)\n   513\u2192\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(refreshDiags)\n   514\u2192\t\t\treturn nil, nil, diags\n   515\u2192\t\t}\n   516\u2192\n   517\u2192\t\t// We'll use the refreshed state -- which is the  \"prior state\" from\n   518\u2192\t\t// the perspective of this \"destroy plan\" -- as the starting state\n   519\u2192\t\t// for our destroy-plan walk, so it can take into account if we\n   520\u2192\t\t// detected during refreshing that anything was already deleted outside\n   521\u2192\t\t// of Terraform.\n   522\u2192\t\tpriorState = refreshPlan.PriorState.DeepCopy()\n   523\u2192\n   524\u2192\t\t// The refresh plan may have upgraded state for some resources, make\n   525\u2192\t\t// sure we store the new version.\n   526\u2192\t\tprevRunState = refreshPlan.PrevRunState.DeepCopy()\n   527\u2192\t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] Context.destroyPlan: now _really_ creating a destroy plan\")\n   528\u2192\t}\n   529\u2192\n   530\u2192\tdestroyPlan, evalScope, walkDiags := c.planWalk(config, priorState, opts)\n   531\u2192\tdiags = diags.Append(walkDiags)\n   532\u2192\tif walkDiags.HasErrors() {\n   533\u2192\t\t// Non-nil plan along with errors indicates a non-applyable partial\n   534\u2192\t\t// plan that's only suitable to be shown to the user as extra context\n   535\u2192\t\t// to help understand the errors.\n   536\u2192\t\treturn destroyPlan, evalScope, diags\n   537\u2192\t}\n   538\u2192\n   539\u2192\tif !opts.SkipRefresh {\n   540\u2192\t\t// If we didn't skip refreshing then we want the previous run state to\n   541\u2192\t\t// be the one we originally fed into the c.refreshOnlyPlan call above,\n   542\u2192\t\t// not the refreshed version we used for the destroy planWalk.\n   543\u2192\t\tdestroyPlan.PrevRunState = prevRunState\n   544\u2192\t}\n   545\u2192\n   546\u2192\trelevantAttrs, rDiags := c.relevantResourceAttrsForPlan(config, destroyPlan)\n   547\u2192\tdiags = diags.Append(rDiags)\n   548\u2192\n   549\u2192\tdestroyPlan.RelevantAttributes = relevantAttrs\n   550\u2192\treturn destroyPlan, evalScope, diags\n   551\u2192}\n   552\u2192\n   553\u2192func (c *Context) prePlanFindAndApplyMoves(config *configs.Config, prevRunState *states.State) ([]refactoring.MoveStatement, refactoring.MoveResults, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n   554\u2192\texplicitMoveStmts := refactoring.FindMoveStatements(config)\n   555\u2192\timplicitMoveStmts := refactoring.ImpliedMoveStatements(config, prevRunState, explicitMoveStmts)\n   556\u2192\tvar moveStmts []refactoring.MoveStatement\n   557\u2192\tif stmtsLen := len(explicitMoveStmts) + len(implicitMoveStmts); stmtsLen > 0 {\n   558\u2192\t\tmoveStmts = make([]refactoring.MoveStatement, 0, stmtsLen)\n   559\u2192\t\tmoveStmts = append(moveStmts, explicitMoveStmts...)\n   560\u2192\t\tmoveStmts = append(moveStmts, implicitMoveStmts...)\n   561\u2192\t}\n   562\u2192\tmoveResults, diags := refactoring.ApplyMoves(moveStmts, prevRunState, c.plugins.ProviderFactories())\n   563\u2192\treturn moveStmts, moveResults, diags\n   564\u2192}\n   565\u2192\n   566\u2192func (c *Context) prePlanVerifyTargetedMoves(moveResults refactoring.MoveResults, targets []addrs.Targetable) tfdiags.Diagnostics {\n   567\u2192\tif len(targets) < 1 {\n   568\u2192\t\treturn nil // the following only matters when targeting\n   569\u2192\t}\n   570\u2192\n   571\u2192\tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n   572\u2192\n   573\u2192\tvar excluded []addrs.AbsResourceInstance\n   574\u2192\tfor _, result := range moveResults.Changes.Values() {\n   575\u2192\t\tfromMatchesTarget := false\n   576\u2192\t\ttoMatchesTarget := false\n   577\u2192\t\tfor _, targetAddr := range targets {\n   578\u2192\t\t\tif targetAddr.TargetContains(result.From) {\n   579\u2192\t\t\t\tfromMatchesTarget = true\n   580\u2192\t\t\t}\n   581\u2192\t\t\tif targetAddr.TargetContains(result.To) {\n   582\u2192\t\t\t\ttoMatchesTarget = true\n   583\u2192\t\t\t}\n   584\u2192\t\t}\n   585\u2192\t\tif !fromMatchesTarget {\n   586\u2192\t\t\texcluded = append(excluded, result.From)\n   587\u2192\t\t}\n   588\u2192\t\tif !toMatchesTarget {\n   589\u2192\t\t\texcluded = append(excluded, result.To)\n   590\u2192\t\t}\n   591\u2192\t}\n   592\u2192\tif len(excluded) > 0 {\n   593\u2192\t\tsort.Slice(excluded, func(i, j int) bool {\n   594\u2192\t\t\treturn excluded[i].Less(excluded[j])\n   595\u2192\t\t})\n   596\u2192\n   597\u2192\t\tvar listBuf strings.Builder\n   598\u2192\t\tvar prevResourceAddr addrs.AbsResource\n   599\u2192\t\tfor _, instAddr := range excluded {\n   600\u2192\t\t\t// Targeting generally ends up selecting whole resources rather\n   601\u2192\t\t\t// than individual instances, because we don't factor in\n   602\u2192\t\t\t// individual instances until DynamicExpand, so we're going to\n   603\u2192\t\t\t// always show whole resource addresses here, excluding any\n   604\u2192\t\t\t// instance keys. (This also neatly avoids dealing with the\n   605\u2192\t\t\t// different quoting styles required for string instance keys\n   606\u2192\t\t\t// on different shells, which is handy.)\n   607\u2192\t\t\t//\n   608\u2192\t\t\t// To avoid showing duplicates when we have multiple instances\n   609\u2192\t\t\t// of the same resource, we'll remember the most recent\n   610\u2192\t\t\t// resource we rendered in prevResource, which is sufficient\n   611\u2192\t\t\t// because we sorted the list of instance addresses above, and\n   612\u2192\t\t\t// our sort order always groups together instances of the same\n   613\u2192\t\t\t// resource.\n   614\u2192\t\t\tresourceAddr := instAddr.ContainingResource()\n   615\u2192\t\t\tif resourceAddr.Equal(prevResourceAddr) {\n   616\u2192\t\t\t\tcontinue\n   617\u2192\t\t\t}\n   618\u2192\t\t\tfmt.Fprintf(&listBuf, \"\\n  -target=%q\", resourceAddr.String())\n   619\u2192\t\t\tprevResourceAddr = resourceAddr\n   620\u2192\t\t}\n   621\u2192\t\tdiags = diags.Append(tfdiags.Sourceless(\n   622\u2192\t\t\ttfdiags.Error,\n   623\u2192\t\t\t\"Moved resource instances excluded by targeting\",\n   624\u2192\t\t\tfmt.Sprintf(\n   625\u2192\t\t\t\t\"Resource instances in your current state have moved to new addresses in the latest configuration. Terraform must include those resource instances while planning in order to ensure a correct result, but your -target=... options do not fully cover all of those resource instances.\\n\\nTo create a valid plan, either remove your -target=... options altogether or add the following additional target options:%s\\n\\nNote that adding these options may include further additional resource instances in your plan, in order to respect object dependencies.\",\n   626\u2192\t\t\t\tlistBuf.String(),\n   627\u2192\t\t\t),\n   628\u2192\t\t))\n   629\u2192\t}\n   630\u2192\n   631\u2192\treturn diags\n   632\u2192}\n   633\u2192\n   634\u2192func (c *Context) postPlanValidateMoves(config *configs.Config, stmts []refactoring.MoveStatement, allInsts instances.Set) tfdiags.Diagnostics {\n   635\u2192\treturn refactoring.ValidateMoves(stmts, config, allInsts)\n   636\u2192}\n   637\u2192\n   638\u2192// findImportTargets builds a list of import targets from any import blocks in\n   639\u2192// config.\n   640\u2192func (c *Context) findImportTargets(config *configs.Config) []*ImportTarget {\n   641\u2192\tvar importTargets []*ImportTarget\n   642\u2192\tfor _, ic := range config.Module.Import {\n   643\u2192\t\timportTargets = append(importTargets, &ImportTarget{\n   644\u2192\t\t\tConfig: ic,\n   645\u2192\t\t})\n   646\u2192\t}\n   647\u2192\treturn importTargets\n   648\u2192}\n   649\u2192\n   650\u2192// findForgetTargets builds a list of resources and a list of modules to be\n   651\u2192// forgotten, based on any removed blocks in config.\n   652\u2192func (c *Context) findForgetTargets(config *configs.Config) (forgetResources []addrs.ConfigResource, forgetModules []addrs.Module, diags tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n   653\u2192\tremoveStmts, diags := refactoring.FindRemoveStatements(config)\n   654\u2192\tif diags.HasErrors() {\n   655\u2192\t\treturn nil, nil, diags\n   656\u2192\t}\n   657\u2192\tfor _, rst := range removeStmts.Values() {\n   658\u2192\t\tif rst.Destroy {\n   659\u2192\t\t\t// no-op\n   660\u2192\t\t} else {\n   661\u2192\t\t\tif fr, ok := rst.From.(addrs.ConfigResource); ok {\n   662\u2192\t\t\t\tforgetResources = append(forgetResources, fr)\n   663\u2192\t\t\t} else if fm, ok := rst.From.(addrs.Module); ok {\n   664\u2192\t\t\t\tforgetModules = append(forgetModules, fm)\n   665\u2192\t\t\t} else {\n   666\u2192\t\t\t\tpanic(\"Invalid ConfigMoveable type in remove statement\")\n   667\u2192\t\t\t}\n   668\u2192\t\t}\n   669\u2192\t}\n   670\u2192\treturn forgetResources, forgetModules, diags\n   671\u2192}\n   672\u2192\n   673\u2192func (c *Context) planWalk(config *configs.Config, prevRunState *states.State, opts *PlanOpts) (*plans.Plan, *lang.Scope, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n   674\u2192\tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n   675\u2192\tlog.Printf(\"[DEBUG] Building and walking plan graph for %s\", opts.Mode)\n   676\u2192\n   677\u2192\tprevRunState = prevRunState.DeepCopy() // don't modify the caller's object when we process the moves\n   678\u2192\tmoveStmts, moveResults, moveDiags := c.prePlanFindAndApplyMoves(config, prevRunState)\n   679\u2192\tdiags = diags.Append(moveDiags)\n   680\u2192\tif moveDiags.HasErrors() {\n   681\u2192\t\treturn nil, nil, diags\n   682\u2192\t}\n   683\u2192\n   684\u2192\t// If resource targeting is in effect then it might conflict with the\n   685\u2192\t// move result.\n   686\u2192\tdiags = diags.Append(c.prePlanVerifyTargetedMoves(moveResults, opts.Targets))\n   687\u2192\tif diags.HasErrors() {\n   688\u2192\t\t// We'll return early here, because if we have any moved resource\n   689\u2192\t\t// instances excluded by targeting then planning is likely to encounter\n   690\u2192\t\t// strange problems that may lead to confusing error messages.\n   691\u2192\t\treturn nil, nil, diags\n   692\u2192\t}\n   693\u2192\n   694\u2192\tgraph, walkOp, moreDiags := c.planGraph(config, prevRunState, opts)\n   695\u2192\tdiags = diags.Append(moreDiags)\n   696\u2192\tif diags.HasErrors() {\n   697\u2192\t\treturn nil, nil, diags\n   698\u2192\t}\n   699\u2192\n   700\u2192\ttimestamp := time.Now().UTC()\n   701\u2192\tif opts.ForcePlanTimestamp != nil {\n   702\u2192\t\t// Some tests use this to produce stable results to assert against.\n   703\u2192\t\ttimestamp = *opts.ForcePlanTimestamp\n   704\u2192\t}\n   705\u2192\n   706\u2192\tvar externalProviderConfigs map[addrs.RootProviderConfig]providers.Interface\n   707\u2192\tif opts != nil {\n   708\u2192\t\texternalProviderConfigs = opts.ExternalProviders\n   709\u2192\t}\n   710\u2192\n   711\u2192\t// If we get here then we should definitely have a non-nil \"graph\", which\n   712\u2192\t// we can now walk.\n   713\u2192\tchanges := plans.NewChanges()\n   714\u2192\n   715\u2192\t// Initialize the results table to validate provider function calls.\n   716\u2192\t// Hold reference to this so we can store the table data in the plan file.\n   717\u2192\tproviderFuncResults := providers.NewFunctionResultsTable(nil)\n   718\u2192\n   719\u2192\twalker, walkDiags := c.walk(graph, walkOp, &graphWalkOpts{\n   720\u2192\t\tConfig:                     config,\n   721\u2192\t\tInputState:                 prevRunState,\n   722\u2192\t\tExternalProviderConfigs:    externalProviderConfigs,\n   723\u2192\t\tDeferralAllowed:            opts.DeferralAllowed,\n   724\u2192\t\tExternalDependencyDeferred: opts.ExternalDependencyDeferred,\n   725\u2192\t\tChanges:                    changes,\n   726\u2192\t\tMoveResults:                moveResults,\n   727\u2192\t\tOverrides:                  opts.Overrides,\n   728\u2192\t\tPlanTimeTimestamp:          timestamp,\n   729\u2192\t\tProviderFuncResults:        providerFuncResults,\n   730\u2192\t\tForget:                     opts.Forget,\n   731\u2192\t})\n   732\u2192\tdiags = diags.Append(walker.NonFatalDiagnostics)\n   733\u2192\tdiags = diags.Append(walkDiags)\n   734\u2192\n   735\u2192\tallInsts := walker.InstanceExpander.AllInstances()\n   736\u2192\n   737\u2192\tmoveValidateDiags := c.postPlanValidateMoves(config, moveStmts, allInsts)\n   738\u2192\tif moveValidateDiags.HasErrors() {\n   739\u2192\t\t// If any of the move statements are invalid then those errors take\n   740\u2192\t\t// precedence over any other errors because an incomplete move graph\n   741\u2192\t\t// is quite likely to be the _cause_ of various errors. This oddity\n   742\u2192\t\t// comes from the fact that we need to apply the moves before we\n   743\u2192\t\t// actually validate them, because validation depends on the result\n   744\u2192\t\t// of first trying to plan.\n   745\u2192\t\treturn nil, nil, moveValidateDiags\n   746\u2192\t}\n   747\u2192\tdiags = diags.Append(moveValidateDiags) // might just contain warnings\n   748\u2192\n   749\u2192\tif moveResults.Blocked.Len() > 0 && !diags.HasErrors() {\n   750\u2192\t\t// If we had blocked moves and we're not going to be returning errors\n   751\u2192\t\t// then we'll report the blockers as a warning. We do this only in the\n   752\u2192\t\t// absense of errors because invalid move statements might well be\n   753\u2192\t\t// the root cause of the blockers, and so better to give an actionable\n   754\u2192\t\t// error message than a less-actionable warning.\n   755\u2192\t\tdiags = diags.Append(blockedMovesWarningDiag(moveResults))\n   756\u2192\t}\n   757\u2192\n   758\u2192\t// If we reach this point with error diagnostics then \"changes\" is a\n   759\u2192\t// representation of the subset of changes we were able to plan before\n   760\u2192\t// we encountered errors, which we'll return as part of a non-nil plan\n   761\u2192\t// so that e.g. the UI can show what was planned so far in case that extra\n   762\u2192\t// context helps the user to understand the error messages we're returning.\n   763\u2192\tprevRunState = walker.PrevRunState.Close()\n   764\u2192\n   765\u2192\t// The refreshed state may have data resource objects which were deferred\n   766\u2192\t// to apply and cannot be serialized.\n   767\u2192\twalker.RefreshState.RemovePlannedResourceInstanceObjects()\n   768\u2192\tpriorState := walker.RefreshState.Close()\n   769\u2192\n   770\u2192\tdriftedResources, driftDiags := c.driftedResources(config, prevRunState, priorState, moveResults)\n   771\u2192\tdiags = diags.Append(driftDiags)\n   772\u2192\n   773\u2192\tdeferredResources, deferredDiags := c.deferredResources(config, walker.Deferrals.GetDeferredChanges(), priorState)\n   774\u2192\tdiags = diags.Append(deferredDiags)\n   775\u2192\n   776\u2192\tvar forgottenResources []string\n   777\u2192\tfor _, rc := range changes.Resources {\n   778\u2192\t\tif rc.Action == plans.Forget {\n   779\u2192\t\t\t// TODO KEM display resource ids\n   780\u2192\t\t\tforgottenResources = append(forgottenResources, fmt.Sprintf(\" - %s\", rc.Addr))\n   781\u2192\t\t}\n   782\u2192\t}\n   783\u2192\tif len(forgottenResources) > 0 {\n   784\u2192\t\tdiags = diags.Append(tfdiags.Sourceless(\n   785\u2192\t\t\ttfdiags.Warning,\n   786\u2192\t\t\t\"Some objects will no longer be managed by Terraform\",\n   787\u2192\t\t\tfmt.Sprintf(\"If you apply this plan, Terraform will discard its tracking information for the following objects, but it will not delete them:\\n%s\\n\\nAfter applying this plan, Terraform will no longer manage these objects. You will need to import them into Terraform to manage them again.\", strings.Join(forgottenResources, \"\\n\")),\n   788\u2192\t\t))\n   789\u2192\t}\n   790\u2192\tschemas, schemaDiags := c.Schemas(config, prevRunState)\n   791\u2192\t// We must finish building a plan object, and cannot return early here.\n   792\u2192\tvar changesSrc *plans.ChangesSrc\n   793\u2192\tvar err error\n   794\u2192\tif !schemaDiags.HasErrors() {\n   795\u2192\t\tchangesSrc, err = changes.Encode(schemas)\n   796\u2192\t\tif err != nil {\n   797\u2192\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(err)\n   798\u2192\t\t}\n   799\u2192\t}\n   800\u2192\n   801\u2192\tplan := &plans.Plan{\n   802\u2192\t\tUIMode:                  opts.Mode,\n   803\u2192\t\tChanges:                 changesSrc,\n   804\u2192\t\tDriftedResources:        driftedResources,\n   805\u2192\t\tDeferredResources:       deferredResources,\n   806\u2192\t\tPrevRunState:            prevRunState,\n   807\u2192\t\tPriorState:              priorState,\n   808\u2192\t\tExternalReferences:      opts.ExternalReferences,\n   809\u2192\t\tOverrides:               opts.Overrides,\n   810\u2192\t\tChecks:                  states.NewCheckResults(walker.Checks),\n   811\u2192\t\tTimestamp:               timestamp,\n   812\u2192\t\tProviderFunctionResults: providerFuncResults.GetHashes(),\n   813\u2192\n   814\u2192\t\t// Other fields get populated by Context.Plan after we return\n   815\u2192\t}\n   816\u2192\n   817\u2192\t// Our final rulings on whether the plan is \"complete\" and \"applyable\".\n   818\u2192\t// See the documentation for these plan fields to learn what exactly they\n   819\u2192\t// are intended to mean.\n   820\u2192\tif !diags.HasErrors() {\n   821\u2192\t\tif len(opts.Targets) == 0 && !walker.Deferrals.HaveAnyDeferrals() {\n   822\u2192\t\t\t// A plan without any targets or deferred actions should be\n   823\u2192\t\t\t// complete if we didn't encounter errors while producing it.\n   824\u2192\t\t\tlog.Println(\"[TRACE] Plan is complete\")\n   825\u2192\t\t\tplan.Complete = true\n   826\u2192\t\t} else {\n   827\u2192\t\t\tlog.Println(\"[TRACE] Plan is incomplete\")\n   828\u2192\t\t}\n   829\u2192\t\tif opts.Mode == plans.RefreshOnlyMode {\n   830\u2192\t\t\t// In refresh-only mode we explicitly don't expect to propose any\n   831\u2192\t\t\t// actions, but the plan is applyable if the state was changed\n   832\u2192\t\t\t// in an interesting way by the refresh step.\n   833\u2192\t\t\tplan.Applyable = Evaluates HCL configuration expressions to get proposed configuration values\n\n2. **ProposedNew Calculation** (line 896)\n   ```go\n   proposedNewVal := objchange.ProposedNew(schema, unmarkedPriorVal, unmarkedConfigVal)\n   ```\n   - Merges prior state and configuration per schema rules\n   - Unmarked values prevent sensitive data disclosure in logs\n\n3. **Provider Validation** (lines 866-875)\n   ```go\n   validateResp := provider.ValidateResourceConfig(\n       providers.ValidateResourceConfigRequest{\n           TypeName: n.Addr.Resource.Resource.Type,\n           Config:   unmarkedConfigVal,\n       },\n   )\n   ```\n   - Allows provider to reject invalid config before planning\n\n4. **ignore_changes Processing** (lines 884-888)\n   - Applies `ignore_changes` attribute to preserve certain fields\n   - Must occur before PlanResourceChange for consistency\n\n5. **PlanResourceChange RPC Call** (lines 927-937)\n   ```go\n   resp = provider.PlanResourceChange(providers.PlanResourceChangeRequest{\n       TypeName:         n.Addr.Resource.Resource.Type,\n       Config:           unmarkedConfigVal,\n       PriorState:       unmarkedPriorVal,\n       ProposedNewState: proposedNewVal,\n       PriorPrivate:     priorPrivate,\n       ProviderMeta:     metaConfigVal,\n       ClientCapabilities: providers.ClientCapabilities{\n           DeferralAllowed: deferralAllowed,\n       },\n   })\n   ```\n   - **File**: `internal/providers/provider.go`\n   - **Request Fields**:\n     - `TypeName`: Resource type (e.g., \"aws_instance\")\n     - `Config`: HCL-evaluated configuration (marked values preserved)\n     - `PriorState`: Current state before change (null for creates)\n     - `ProposedNewState`: Theoretical new state from config\n     - `PriorPrivate`: Provider-managed sensitive data from prior state\n     - `ProviderMeta`: terraform_data values if present\n     - `ClientCapabilities.DeferralAllowed`: If deferrals permitted\n   - **Response Processing**:\n     - `resp.PlannedState`: Provider's computed new state (line 954)\n     - `resp.PlannedPrivate`: Provider's sensitive data for new state (line 955)\n     - `resp.Deferred`: Optional deferral directive (line 951)\n     - `resp.Diagnostics`: Provider warnings/errors\n\n6. **Action Determination** (lines 1042-1150, not shown in excerpt but referenced)\n   - Provider's response implicitly determines action:\n     - **Create** (`plans.Create`): `PriorState` is null, `PlannedState` is non-null\n     - **Update** (`plans.Update`): Both prior and planned differ with same values for unchanged attributes\n     - **Replace** (`plans.Replace`): Fields marked with `RequiresReplace` in schema are changed\n     - **Delete** (`plans.Delete`): Only computed during destroy plans (not here)\n     - **NoOp** (`plans.NoOp`): Prior and planned states are identical\n\n7. **Force-Replace Override** (lines 388-395 in managedResourceExecute)\n   - If resource addr in `n.forceReplace`:\n     - Planned action is upgraded to Replace if it was NoOp or Update\n     - Change.ActionReason set to `plans.ResourceInstanceReplaceByTriggers` (line 394)\n\n8. **Deferred Actions** (lines 397-476 in managedResourceExecute)\n   - If provider returned `resp.Deferred`:\n     - Change stored in deferrals tracker (line 402)\n     - Not added to plan yet; will be revisited after dependencies resolve\n   - If dependent resource was deferred:\n     - This resource also deferred (line 475)\n\n9. **Change Persistence** (lines 424-431 in managedResourceExecute)\n   - Write computed change to plan via `n.writeChange(ctx, change, \"\")` (line 424)\n   - Write resulting state via `n.writeResourceInstanceState(ctx, instancePlanState, workingState)` (line 428)\n\n### Refresh vs Plan Comparison\n\n**Refresh** (`n.refresh()` - line 298):\n- Calls provider's `ReadResource` RPC with current state ID\n- Returns actual remote resource attributes\n- Detects out-of-band changes and deletions\n- State is updated to reflect upstream reality\n\n**Plan** (`n.plan()` - lines 354-356):\n- Compares refreshed state (prior) with desired configuration\n- Calls provider's `PlanResourceChange` RPC\n- Provider determines if attributes require replacement or can be updated in-place\n- Produces ResourceInstanceChange with proposed action and new value\n\n### Summary: Action Determination Logic\n\nThe provider's `PlanResourceChange` determines the action by:\n1. Analyzing which configuration attributes changed from prior state\n2. For changed attributes, checking schema's `RequiresReplace` directive\n3. Returning PlannedState with sensitive fields computed\n4. Terraform Core calculates action based on schema-governed requirements\n\nThe complete resource change is captured in `plans.ResourceInstanceChange`:\n- `Addr`: Resource address\n- `ProviderAddr`: Provider configuration used\n- `Change.Action`: Create/Update/Replace/Delete/NoOp\n- `Change.Before`: Prior state value\n- `Change.After`: Planned new value\n- `Change.Importing`: If this is an import operation\n- `ActionReason`: Why action was chosen (e.g., RequiresReplace, ForcedReplace, TriggeredBy)\n\n## Evidence\n\n### Key File Paths and Line References\n\n**Command Layer**:\n- `internal/command/plan.go:22-118` - PlanCommand.Run() Entry Point** (`internal/command/plan.go:22`)\n- Parses CLI arguments using `arguments.ParsePlan(rawArgs)` (line 34)\n- Prepares the backend via `c.PrepareBackend()` (line 68)\n- Builds operation request via `c.OperationRequest()` (line 82)\n  - Sets `opReq.Type = backendrun.OperationTypePlan` (line 165)\n  - Configures key fields from `arguments.Operation`:\n    - `opReq.PlanMode = args.PlanMode` (line 158)\n    - `opReq.Targets = args.Targets` (line 163)\n    - `opReq.ForceReplace = args.ForceReplace` (line 164)\n- Invokes `c.RunOperation(be, opReq)` (line 103) which delegates to the backend\n\n**2. Backend Delegation**\n- The backend (typically local backend in `internal/backend/local`) receives the `Operation` request\n- Backend calls `terraform.NewContext()` to instantiate the planning context\n- Backend invokes `context.Plan(config, prevRunState, opts)` where opts is a `*PlanOpts` struct\n\n**3. PlanOpts Structure** (`internal/terraform/context_plan.go:32-138`)\nKey fields controlling plan behavior:\n- `Mode plans.Mode` (line 36) - Specifies plan type: NormalMode, DestroyMode, or RefreshOnlyMode\n- `SkipRefresh bool` (line 42) - Whether to skip refreshing managed resource instances\n- `Targets []addrs.Targetable` (line 68) - Resource instances to limit planning to\n- `ForceReplace []addrs.AbsResourceInstance` (line 79) - Resource instances to force replacement for\n- `DeferralAllowed bool` (line 90) - Whether plan can defer some actions\n- `ExternalProviders map[addrs.RootProviderConfig]providers.Interface` (line 125) - Pre-configured providers passed from caller\n- `Overrides *mocking.Overrides` (line 106) - Testing overrides for provider computed values\n\n**4. **File**: `internal/terraform/transform_config.go`\n   - **Role**: Creates all resource nodes from configuration\n   - Recursively walks the configuration tree adding nodes for:\n     - Managed resources (line 97-99 in transform_config.go)\n     - # Terraform Plan/Apply Pipeline Architecture

## Q1: Command to Context

### Command Execution Flow

The `terraform plan` command is implemented in `internal/command/plan.go` and follows this execution path:

**1. PlanCommand.Run() Entry Point** (`internal/command/plan.go:22`)
- Parses CLI arguments using `arguments.ParsePlan(rawArgs)` (line 34)
- Prepares the backend via `c.PrepareBackend()` (line 68)
- Builds operation request via `c.OperationRequest()` (line 82)
  - Sets `opReq.Type = backendrun.OperationTypePlan` (line 165)
  - Configures key fields from `arguments.Operation`:
    - `opReq.PlanMode = args.PlanMode` (line 158)
    - `opReq.Targets = args.Targets` (line 163)
    - `opReq.ForceReplace = args.ForceReplace` (line 164)
- Invokes `c.RunOperation(be, opReq)` (line 103) which delegates to the backend

**2. Backend Delegation**
- The backend (typically local backend in `internal/backend/local`) receives the `Operation` request
- Backend calls `terraform.NewContext()` to instantiate the planning context
- Backend invokes `context.Plan(config, prevRunState, opts)` where opts is a `*PlanOpts` struct

**3. PlanOpts Structure** (`internal/terraform/context_plan.go:32-138`)
Key fields controlling plan behavior:
- `Mode plans.Mode` (line 36) - Specifies plan type: NormalMode, DestroyMode, or RefreshOnlyMode
- `SkipRefresh bool` (line 42) - Whether to skip refreshing managed resource instances
- `Targets []addrs.Targetable` (line 68) - Resource instances to limit planning to
- `ForceReplace []addrs.AbsResourceInstance` (line 79) - Resource instances to force replacement for
- `DeferralAllowed bool` (line 90) - Whether plan can defer some actions
- `ExternalProviders map[addrs.RootProviderConfig]providers.Interface` (line 125) - Pre-configured providers passed from ca

2. WRITE /logs/agent/sessions/projects/-workspace/memory/MEMORY.md
# Terraform Codebase Architecture Notes

## Plan Execution Pipeline

### High-Level Flow
1. **CLI Entry**: `PlanCommand.Run()` in `internal/command/plan.go`
2. **Backend**: Creates `terraform.Context` and invokes `context.Plan(config, prevRunState, opts)`
3. **Graph Building**: `PlanGraphBuilder.Build()` creates dependency graph using sequence of `GraphTransformer` stages
4. **Graph Walking**: `context.walk()` concurrently executes graph nodes, calling provider RPCs
5. **Result**: Returns `plans.Plan` with `ResourceInstanceChange` objects

### Key Interfaces and Patterns

**PlanOpts Structure** (`context_plan.go:32-138`)
- Controls: Mode (Normal/Destroy/RefreshOnly), SkipRefresh, Targets, ForceReplace, DeferralAllowed
- External providers can be pre-configured and passed in (not configured by Terraform Core)

**GraphTransformer Pipeline** (`graph_builder_plan.go:121-277`)
Order matters:
1. ConfigTransformer - creates resource nodes
2. RootVariableTransformer - adds variable nodes
3. AttachSchemaTransformer - must precede ReferenceTransformer
4. ReferenceTransformer - analyzes and connects references
5. AttachStateTransformer - attaches prior state to nodes
6. Provider transformers - adds provider nodes
7. TargetsTransformer - filters based on `-target`
8. CloseProviderTransformer - adds cleanup nodes

### Provider Lifecycle

**Initialization** → **Configuration** → **Resource Operations** → **Close**

1. `NodeApplyableProvider.Execute()` calls:
   - `ctx.InitProvider()` - instantiates provider plugin via plugin factory
   - `ctx.ConfigureProvider()` - calls provider's ConfigureProvider RPC
2. Resource nodes use provider from context cache
3. `CloseProviderTransformer` adds nodes to close connections at end

### Resource Planning

**Single Resource Flow**: `NodePlannable
... (truncated)
